# Supported Features
- Imported stage layers expose bounded `scalestart`, `scaledelta`, and
  scalar-or-pair `zoomdelta` projection for normal, animated, asset, and
  placeholder backgrounds. Deprecated `yscalestart`/`yscaledelta` use the
  documented bounded reciprocal vertical scale when general scale is absent.
  Sprite dimensions scale around the authored SFF axis; explicit zoomdelta is
  compensated against the global Three.js camera. Exact parallax deformation,
  legacy `xscale`, window/mask zoom,
  camera-anchor/localcoord normalization, and full MUGEN/IKEMEN stage parity
  remain unsupported.
- Imported stage layers preserve bounded `positionlink` target/offset metadata,
  inherit the linked scroll delta, and follow the target's same-tick bounded
  motion/visibility in the immutable stage projection. Exact shared BGCtrl
  state across linked groups, all-target ordering, and full stage parity remain
  unsupported.

- Explicit IKEMEN snapshots and trace frames publish
  `RuntimeAuxiliaryResourceProjection/v0` for roots and live Helpers with
  actor-local owner ids, red-life, guard-point, and dizzy-point values/maxima,
  suppression status, deterministic ordering, and finite/max diagnostics.
  Projectile/Explod actors are excluded and the projection is outside behavior
  checksums. The separate `RuntimeRedLifeShareSystem/v0` adapter now mirrors
  imported root red-life through a team bank when IKEMEN `TeamLifeShare` is
  enabled, while local mode stays actor-owned; positive values clamp from
  current life to life max and KO clears the side. The imported direct-hit
  dizzy break route can enter the available common `StateDizzy` state after a
  positive-to-zero crossing. Typed team handoff reconciles the red-life bank
  immediately and match reset rebinds it from the representative root.
  Red-life triggers, projectile/Explod/team-helper sharing, exact multi-round
  persistence, HUD bars, and full parity remain separate gates.

- Imported runtime supports the bounded explicit direct HitDef `redlife` and
  `guardpoints`/`dizzypoints` routes plus actor-local `RedLifeAdd`/`RedLifeSet`,
  `GuardPointsAdd`/`GuardPointsSet`, and `DizzyPointsAdd`/`DizzyPointsSet`,
  including authored-max/life fallback, omitted normal/Super HitDef defaults,
  dedicated `AttackMulSet.DizzyPoints` scaling, signed scaling, clamps, and
  required trace evidence. A bounded imported direct HitDef crossing can enter
  the available common `StateDizzy` route when no explicit `p2stateno` owns the
  hit. Root `TeamLifeShare` is covered only by the separate imported adapter;
  Helpers retain local controller ownership. Native red-life triggers,
  target/projectile sharing, exact multi-round persistence, HUD presentation,
  and full parity remain unsupported; defender-owned `NoDizzyPointsDamage`
  suppression is bounded.

- Legal-fixture browser smoke proves one lethal imported `AssertSpecial NoKOSlow` route: physical `d -> z` enters imported state/action `210`, asserts `nokoslow` on the KO tick, defeats demo Nova Boxer from `1000` to `0`, retains post-round playback `1`, and returns to a healthy `fight` round after Reset. Desktop/mobile captures require the imported identity, action-specific palette/mask, `RuntimePostRound.noKoSlow`, progress, and normal playback. Required `mugen-lite-journey-nokoslow` trace checksum `ceac9f37` independently proves the legal ZIP command/state/AIR/SFF path. Exact slowdown curve/duration, motif/lifebar behavior, KO echoes, win/continue flow, teams, broad audio parity, and full round parity remain separate gates.

- Legal-fixture browser smoke proves one two-element imported AIR attack: real keyboard `a -> x`, action `200` sprite `200,0` then `200,1`, action-palette crop evidence, distinct masks, and idle return on desktop/mobile. Required trace evidence separately records action-`200` AIR elements `0` and `1` with per-element frame counts; unqualified `minFrames` aggregation remains unchanged. AIR loop semantics, loopstart, interpolation, arbitrary timing/offset/flip/trans parameters, multi-frame coverage beyond this action, production art, and visual parity remain separate gates.

- Legal-fixture browser smoke proves a zero-chip imported guard contact for this fixture matchup: exact imported P1/demo Nova Boxer AI P2 roster, native AI attack window, held ArrowLeft, imported state/action `150`, `guarding=true`, life `1000`, visible sprite frame `150,0`, and idle return on desktop/mobile. Nonzero chip formulas, exact timing/slide, crouch/air guard, body-push, multi-hit, touch input, production art, and visual parity remain separate gates.

- Legal-fixture browser smoke proves the fixture CNS recovery command: exact imported P1/demo Nova Boxer AI P2 roster, native AI hit, `5000 -> 5050 -> 5100`, two real UI frame steps, fresh keyboard `a+s -> x+y`, imported `5200`, and idle return. Desktop/mobile crops require action-palette evidence and distinct masks. Common1 recovery tables/thresholds, body-push, multi-hit, touch input, production art, and visual parity remain separate gates.

- Legal-fixture browser smoke swaps demo Nova Boxer P1/imported MUGEN-lite P2 through real Match selects, verifies exact roster ids plus actor identities, approaches to bounded center distance, attacks with keyboard `a`, and requires imported get-hit/fall states `5000 -> 5050 -> 5100`, damage `1000 -> 945`, action-palette crop evidence, distinct masks, and natural idle return on desktop/mobile. Body-push semantics, guard visuals, repeated hits, production art, and visual parity remain separate gates.

- Legal-fixture browser smoke drives ArrowRight, ArrowDown, and ArrowUp through the production keyboard adapter and requires imported walk `20`, crouch `10`, and jump `40` poses. Each desktop/mobile crop contains its action-specific palette, differs spatially from idle, and returns to state/action `0/0`. Backward/diagonal movement, guard/recovery visuals, touch input, multi-frame movement actions, production art, and visual parity remain separate gates.

- Legal-fixture browser smoke proves a real keyboard `a` press emits MUGEN command `x`, enters imported state/action `200`, renders palette-backed attack silhouettes for `200,0` then `200,1`, and returns to state/action `0`. Camera-aware spatial mask checksums cover desktop and mobile independently. Full combat/recovery journeys, multi-frame actions beyond this legal fixture route, visual contact proof, touch input, production art, and visual parity remain separate gates.

- Browser smoke generates and independently uploads the repository-owned legal MUGEN-lite ZIP through the real file input at desktop/mobile viewports, enters Match with the imported fighter, and requires Three.js to present frame `0,0` as `32x64@16,62`. Camera-aware P1 crops must contain fixture-palette pixels; full canvases must remain nonblank. Production art, production-host smoke, public character compatibility, and visual parity remain separate gates.

- The repository-owned legal MUGEN-lite package contains thirteen visible 32x64 indexed PCX frames in SFF v1 with foot-aligned axes and distinct movement/combat/recovery geometry, including both action-`200` elements. Loader tests prove decoded dimensions, axes, unique indexed payloads, terrestrial baseline contact, airborne separation, and no pixels below the axis. Pose-transition rendering, production art quality, multi-frame animation beyond action `200`, palette breadth, and visual parity remain separate gates.

- Local ZIP ingestion publishes `ZipCharacterSourcePolicy/v0`: 256 MiB compressed, 4,096 archive entries, 64 MiB per expanded file, and 512 MiB total expanded bytes by default. Invalid archives or entry streams, sanitized traversal, absolute/drive/NUL paths, and case-insensitive virtual-path collisions fail with typed errors; actual extracted bytes are rechecked sequentially and UI rejection is logged. This is defense in depth for local package loading, not antivirus, parser isolation, metadata-free pre-decompression guarantees, password/multivolume support, or complete sandbox security.

- Explicit IKEMEN snapshots expose renderer-independent `RuntimeRootPresentation/v1`: one stable draw/camera/collision-debug reason row per root plus ordered consumer ids. Explicit Tag collision debug admits valid non-disabled/non-standby player roots independently from `AssertSpecial invisible` and `ScreenBound moveCameraX`; Three.js strictly resolves ids across pair/reserve storage and keeps effect overlays unchanged. Required checksum `97255586` plus desktop/mobile smoke prove `[p1,p2] -> [p3,p2] -> [p1,p2]` body/camera/collision handoff/reset, exact collision actors, two boxes, stable HUD, and no stale mesh. Presentation remains independent from newer active-root direct combat; HUD/audio playback, team round, and shared resources remain pair-owned.

- Explicit IKEMEN `MatchWorldActorRegistrySnapshot.rootPhaseCapabilities` exposes `RuntimeRootPhaseCapabilities/v5`. It reconciles live team state, participation, input routing, presentation, constraints, body push, hit admission, effect-store ownership, and direct-combat participation. `RuntimeRootDirectHitAdmission/v1` validates root identity, sorts ReversalDef getters before HitDef getters and PlayerNo, and traverses admitted mutation getter-first. Explicit Tag arbitrates every unordered admitted pair through typed `Hit | Miss | Dodge` HitDef priority before actor-generic direct mutation. Equal Hit/Hit graph edges batch bilateral contacts; Hit beats Miss; Dodge-related and other non-Hit ties skip both directions only for that frame. Pair consumes the same equal-priority outcomes before its legacy directed combat calls. Required five-root Tag evidence proves active P4 ReversalDef counters P5 before competing P2 HitDef can interrupt P5. Required active-root HitOverride evidence proves P3 can program one ordinary defender-owned slot and redirect P4's admitted direct HitDef without normal damage. Direct native input/AI, exact AffectTeam/Y/Z/localcoord/juggle, ReversalDef-versus-ReversalDef ordering, broad HitOverride variants/guard interaction, throws, round, and shared resources remain blocked for P3-P8.
- The same admission snapshot exposes dual-ReversalDef candidates in separate `reversalClashDecisions` and `admittedReversalClashPairIds` fields. Getter order, stable attacker order, activity, enemy side, reversal attr, and Clsn1 contact are trace-gated. Explicit Tag consumes candidates before HitDef priority: the first directed pair applies attacker-owned reversal state, target id, hitpause, power, MoveReversed, reverser/getter reciprocal HitDef contact memory, and move interruption; the inverse stale pair cannot mutate again. Broader tie/randomness, attack depth/Z, AffectTeam, projectile/helper clashes, advanced state ownership, and full parity remain unsupported.

- Explicit IKEMEN Tag normal ticks snapshot every root as `playable`, `active-motion`, or `bounded-standby` before actor execution. `active-motion` advances state time, permits bounded state/Tag/variable/control/no-op, local kinematic controllers, direct `HitDef`/`ReversalDef`, and ordinary actor-local `HitOverride`, then runs local kinematics and animation. Active-root HitOverride slots age once before that root's state/controller phase. Other side-effect routes remain blocked. Active roots participate in stage clamp, body push, hit admission, typed priority, getter-first reversal ordering, and ordered direct mutation; required evidence covers unequal winner suppression, reciprocal Hit/Hit damage, Hit/Miss unilateral contact, Hit/Dodge repeated no-contact, a competing five-root ReversalDef route, and P3/P4 HitOverride redirect. Helper/Projectile/Explod combat, Pause/SuperPause widening, ReversalDef-versus-ReversalDef, broad HitOverride variants/guard interaction, team round, HUD, and shared resources remain blocked.

- Explicit `ikemen-go` `teamMode: "tag"` publishes `RuntimeRootInputRouting/v0`. On normal active ticks, P1 command input is cloned into each valid odd-PlayerNo root buffer and P2 into each valid even-root buffer before controller execution; buffers are independent and update once. Legacy/unknown/Single modes remain pair-only, invalid/disabled/non-player roots fail closed, and Pause/hitpause retain the existing pair path. Direct input/AI and full playable fighter phases remain P1/P2-only; active P3-P8 may independently author bounded CNS HitDef and enter direct combat. Round, HUD/audio playback, and shared resources remain pair-owned.

- `MatchWorldActorRegistrySnapshot.rootParticipation` exposes JSON-safe `RuntimeRootParticipation/v0` diagnostics for all owned roots. Owned, disabled, standby, structurally active, scheduled, input-owned, combat-owned, round-owned, presented, and effect-store-owned are separate fields. Explicit IKEMEN P3-P8 roots now own exact registered effect stores while input/combat/round and effect lifecycle/presentation execution remain pair-only. `effects = true` in the current phase capability means store ownership only; it does not grant playable team support or effect execution.
- Explicit Tag normal post-fighter target maintenance now selects stable unique P1-P8 roots with valid player identity, ages each actor-local target store once, clears stale binding-subject telemetry across all authoritative roots, and resolves existing TargetBind then BindToTarget passes against complete exact-id candidates. Standby and over-KO roots retain maintenance; disabled, non-player, invalid-id, and duplicate roots fail closed. Pair/Single and pause/hitpause preserve prior scheduling. This is maintenance of existing refs/bindings, not deferred hit-target acquisition, target-controller widening, or active-root combat.
- `RuntimeHitDefContactMemory/v0` exposes detached committed/pending getter ids for every root. Accepted direct hit/guard/HitOverride and direct ReversalDef append pending ids while CNS target refs remain immediate; plural priority buffers exact loser-to-winner suppression; active post-combat commits roots in stable order; MoveStart/HitDef/ReversalDef reset both lists. Root admission rejects exact contacted getters instead of treating one scalar contact as every opponent. Legacy pair actors retain scalar compatibility. Projectile/Helper routes, exact hitonce/juggle/priority-type/ReversalDef parity, pause/hitpause commit, and team round/resource ownership remain unsupported.

- Explicit `ikemen-go` host/test commands can atomically update root standby flags after validating the complete batch. `activeRootIdsBySide` projects plural, stable-order structural activation without moving reserves into playable arrays or widening any executable consumer. Invalid targets leave all roots unchanged and reset restores authored standby state. This host/test API remains separate from the bounded root-only CNS Tag/RedirectID route below and does not itself grant playable team behavior.

- `MatchWorldActorRegistrySnapshot.rootSelection` exposes `RuntimeRootSelection/v0`: complete same-side Partner root ids, active opposing Enemy root ids, and stricter P2 candidate ids are separate stable-order lists per root. Enemy retains active over-KO roots while P2 excludes them; Helpers are excluded from this root-only matrix. Automatic expression/gameplay consumption, Partner redirects, and nearest-distance P2 ordering remain unsupported at this layer.

- `RuntimeExpressionContextWorld` can consume a complete actor registry plus one `RuntimeRootSelection/v0` row. Enemy ids feed nearest-ordered `EnemyNear(n)` and `NumEnemy`; P2 candidate ids independently feed P2 state/name/author/distance reads. Explicit empty candidates fail closed, while omitted selection preserves legacy 1v1 behavior. Partner redirect grammar, automatic match-loop wiring, standby CNS execution, and redirected mutation remain unsupported.

- `RuntimeRootCnsExecutionWorld` owns explicit playable, active-motion, and standby controller capability profiles. Controller dispatch blocks state, runtime-controller types, side-effect routes, or unsupported handling before hooks. Non-standby P1/P2 use full playable profile. Standby roots use bounded state/control/state-type/turn/variable/no-op routes. Already-live explicit-Tag P3-P8 add local kinematic controllers plus direct `hitdef` and `reversaldef` side-effect routes. Life/power controllers, Helper/Projectile/Explod, Target, Pause, audio, environment, and sprite effects remain blocked.
- Parameterless self-only `TagIn` and `TagOut` compile into typed `team-standby` operations and mutate only the caller under the explicit IKEMEN profile. Later roots resolve live Enemy/P2 selection in the same tick. This caller-only form does not infer a partner transition.
- Static non-negative Tag `partner` is also supported as a partner-only mutation. Selection advances cyclically through stable same-side root slots and excludes helpers/opponents; missing targets fail closed. Dynamic partner is covered below; self/state/control/member/leader each have separately bounded forms. Gameplay participation remains unsupported.

- Explicit `ikemen-go` RunOrder includes P3-P8 roots in active and pause branches. Standby roots advance state time under bounded CNS and emit only `fighter:controllers`. On normal explicit-Tag ticks, roots already non-standby at pass start use `active-motion`, then kinematics, animation, constraints, body push, hit admission, plural HitDef priority, and bounded direct combat. Pause/hitpause do not promote them. Auto-guard, direct native input/AI, broad effect lifecycle, projectile/helper combat, exact priority-type/ReversalDef parity, round, and shared resources remain P1/P2-owned or blocked. TagIn/TagOut support remains bounded as documented below.
- Explicit IKEMEN `teamMode: "tag"` publishes `RuntimeTagTeamOrder/v0`, keeping stable side-local root slots, mutable member order, and leader identity separate. The model supports atomic order swap/leader rotation, dead-member sinking, deterministic reset, and bounded static/dynamic `memberno` plus TagIn `leader` controller consumption. Single mode exposes no Tag order. Scheduler, selection, gameplay, and rendering do not consume it.
- Static positive TagIn/TagOut `memberno` swaps the caller with a one-based mutable member position only in explicit Tag mode. Bounded dynamic integer expressions use caller context and truncation before the same validation. Invalid positions and non-Tag mode fail before all Tag state/control/standby mutations. Stable root slots, leader identity, scheduler, selection, gameplay, and rendering remain unchanged.
- Static positive TagIn `leader` maps one-based stable PlayerNo to a same-side root only in explicit Tag mode. Bounded dynamic integer expressions use caller context and truncation before the same stable-id validation; rotation uses live life and updates leader/order atomically. Root-to-Helper RedirectID can compose the same stable-root-relative leader rotation. TagOut leader, Helper-authored aggregate controllers, authored initial order, and gameplay/scheduler/selection/render consumption remain unsupported.
- TagIn/TagOut `self` supports bounded runtime boolean expressions against caller CNS context. Zero is false, non-zero is true, values re-evaluate each tick, and malformed structure fails compilation. Root RedirectID retains caller-context evaluation; Helper RedirectID admits false self for local state/control-only mutation and true/default self for standby mutation after local validation.
- TagIn/TagOut `partner` supports bounded runtime integer expressions. Caller-context values truncate toward zero before cyclic same-side selection; authored partner presence preserves omitted-self defaults. Negative and missing-target paths fail atomically.
- TagIn caller `ctrl` supports bounded runtime boolean expressions. Resolution occurs before aggregate mutation, but application remains after caller state entry so explicit control overrides StateDef metadata. Root RedirectID and Helper-local RedirectID are supported; standby then projects effective `Ctrl = 0` without clearing the stored flag.
- TagIn `partnerctrl` supports bounded runtime boolean expressions with a static or bounded dynamic partner ordinal. Resolution precedes aggregate validation; application remains after partner state entry. Root RedirectID selects partner relative to the resolved root; Helper targets remain unsupported.
- TagIn/TagOut caller `stateno` supports bounded runtime integer expressions. Resolution uses original-caller context and integer truncation before the resolved root's own-state availability check; negative or unavailable results fail atomically.
- TagIn/TagOut `partnerstateno` supports bounded runtime integer expressions with a static or bounded dynamic partner ordinal. Resolution uses original-caller context; partner-owned state availability relative to the resolved root is validated before standby, state, or control mutation. Negative, unavailable, and missing-partner paths fail atomically.
- RedirectID research is source-pinned: IKEMEN evaluates an optional integer expression in caller context, resolves a global numeric root/Helper PlayerID before the Tag parameter pass, and applies later mutations to that character. Explicit `ikemen-go` TagIn/TagOut resolve `redirectid` first through the global numeric registry, including opponent/standby roots and live Helpers, while every later Tag expression remains owned by the original caller. Roots retain aggregate prevalidated mutation. Helpers admit local state/control and true/default self standby after validation. Invalid lookup aborts before later expression evaluation or mutation; Helper aggregate axes, generic controller redirects, and exact incremental partial-mutation parity remain unsupported.
- Explicit `ikemen-go` matches integrate `RuntimeCharacterIdentityWorld` across present P1-P8 roots and root-created Helpers. One-based PlayerNo stays separate from stable string actor/effect serial ids; root PlayerID allocates from baseline `56` in present odd-then-even order and each Helper receives the next global ID before same-tick execution. Helpers inherit root PlayerNo plus explicit parent/root PlayerID links. All world-owned expiry, destroy, removal, capacity, and reset routes unregister Helpers; IDs do not recycle inside an identity epoch, while match reset rebuilds the official-style epoch from baseline and preserves root values. `PlayableMatchRuntime.getCharacterIdentity()` exposes detached, deeply frozen `RuntimeCharacterIdentity/v0` diagnostics with root/parent links. Helper self/Parent/Root `ID` and `PlayerNo` execute from explicit fields; `mugen-1.1` creates no profile-owned registry. Helper-created Helpers, Helper-authored RedirectID/aggregate Tag, broad gameplay participation, and score movement remain unsupported.
- Helper Tag RedirectID and standby participation execute as a bounded subset. A root caller may target a live Helper and compose Helper-local state/control/self with stable-root-relative partner, member, and TagIn leader effects under complete local prevalidation. Root-created Helpers also accept bounded static/dynamic initial standby. Unredirected Helper-authored TagIn/TagOut admits only omitted/static/deferred self, mutating local standby with concrete root-owner/Helper-state telemetry. Effective `Ctrl` reads false without clearing stored control and direct Helper HitDef is suppressed until TagIn; CNS/state time, Helper projectiles, targets, identity, animation, snapshots, and drawing remain active. Helper-authored RedirectID/partner/state/control/member/leader, custom-state ownership, incoming Helper hurt/push/camera/opponent breadth, exact incremental partial failure, and legacy remain blocked.
- Required `synthetic-imported-ikemen-helper-self-tag.json` checksum `08014285` proves one Helper-authored default-self TagOut/TagIn cycle with ordered standby/effective-control evidence, continued CNS into state `1283`, concrete `team-standby:*` telemetry, and a preserved Helper-parented Projectile. Literal frame checksums are `17bffcaa`, `750da07e`, `6cde1d19`, and `910fa3f3`; this does not grant active P3-P8 gameplay or broader Helper-authored Tag axes.

- IKEMEN root-player RunOrder is `executed-partial` behind explicit match `runtimeProfile = "ikemen-go"`: two roots consume previous-tick exclusive `RunFirst` / `RunLast`, then use MoveType `A > I > H` and lower id. Their one-based sorted index is exposed through the `RunOrder` trigger before frame controllers. Required traces gate both run flags and `RunOrder = 1` CNS routing. `mugen-1.1` and `unknown` preserve pair order and expose no profile-specific index. Helpers, teams, simul/tag, and full IKEMEN actor scheduling remain unsupported.

- Player `SprPriority` is `rendered-partial` at L2: static/dynamic controller values clamp to official `-5..5` and effective Three.js z puts higher priorities in front. HitDef pair priorities, equal ties, Explod ontop, stage occlusion, and full draw-order parity remain unsupported.

- Player sprite axis projection is `rendered-partial` at proof ladder L2: effective Three.js mesh position/scale matches SFF axis, AIR offset, facing, and runtime scale in desktop/mobile browser oracles. Flips, rotation pivots, draw order, full effects, and reference parity remain unsupported.

- Studio single-match scene authoring is `executed-partial`: name, P1, CPU, and stage edits have explicit dirty state, output invalidation, bounded undo/redo, dirty-navigation protection, debounced local autosave, local save, reload/reopen persistence, versioned project-index migration, and same-origin external revision detection with stale-save rejection, remote reload, and local-copy preservation. Filesystem/source writes and multi-scene graphs remain unsupported.

- Studio project identity authoring is `executed-partial`: project names can be edited, validated, propagated to manifests, autosaved locally, explicitly saved, reopened after reload, and guarded by per-project storage revisions, reloaded from a remote revision, or preserved as a new local project copy. File-system writes and scene/state/collision editors remain unsupported.

- Automatic KO sound is `executed-partial`: first KO transition emits common `f:11,0` per defeated player; time-over emits none; tick-active global `NoKOSnd` suppresses all KO emission. Post-KO echo timing, slowdown, teams, and full round/audio parity remain unsupported.

- Contextual SND selection is `executed-partial`: unprefixed `PlaySnd` uses player SND; unprefixed `HitDef`/`SuperPause` use common prefix `f`; explicit `S`/`F` remain stable; absent common archives fail closed. Full audio ownership/parity remains unsupported.

## Loader

- ZIP packages.
- Browser folder input.
- `.def` discovery in root or nested character folder.
- Case-insensitive virtual path resolution.
- UTF-8/BOM text decoding with Windows-1252 fallback.
- Optional `data/fight.def` discovery for system presentation assets. `[Files] fightfx.air` and `fightfx.sff` are resolved relative to `fight.def`, with basename fallback to `fightfx.air` / `fightfx.sff` when refs are omitted. Parsed FightFX AIR actions are exposed as both `fightfx` and current common/default hit-spark libraries, and decoded FightFX SFF sprites are registered through a global `SffSpriteProvider` route when available. This is first-pass system spark asset plumbing, not full motif/screenpack parsing or exact MUGEN system-asset ownership.

## DEF

- `[Info]`: `name`, `displayname`, `versiondate`, `mugenversion`, `ikemenversion`, `author`.
- `[Info] fightfx.prefix` is preserved from raw sections and handed to imported runtime fighter definitions as lowercase `fightFxPrefix` metadata for bounded FightFX spark and sound trace/debug routing. When `[Files] fx = ...` declares an IKEMEN-style FightFX DEF with matching `[Info] prefix`, that package AIR/SFF/SND is loaded and preferred for runtime `F` spark frames and `F` sound refs before the global `data/fightfx.*` fallback. Exact `sys.ffx` cache/refcount semantics, channel fallback, screenpack ownership, scale, palette, timing, layering, mixing, and full FightFX parity remain unsupported.
- `[Files]`: `cmd`, `cns`, `st`, `stcommon`, `sprite`, `anim`, `sound`, `pal1` through `pal12`.
- Raw sections and diagnostics.

## AIR

- `[Begin Action N]`.
- Frames: `group, image, x, y, time`, optional `flip`, optional `blend`.
- `Loopstart`.
- `Clsn1`, `Clsn2`, `Clsn1Default`, `Clsn2Default`.

## SFF

- Header/version detection.
- Initial SFF v1 subfile parsing.
- Initial 8-bit, single-plane PCX RLE decoding.
- SFF v1 palette propagation for normal and previous-palette sprites.
- SFF v1 `samePalette` PCX subfiles without embedded palette blocks decode against the previous palette instead of truncating the RLE stream.
- Linked SFF v1 sprite records.
- Decoded SFF v1 sprites are exposed through `SffSpriteProvider` and can render in Inspector Mode.
- SFF v2 header, sprite table, palette table, format counts, and palette records.
- SFF v2 RAW8/RAW24/RAW32 decoding.
- SFF v2 RLE8 indexed-sprite decoding.
- SFF v2 RLE5 and LZ5 5-bit indexed-sprite decoding.
- Decoded indexed SFF v1/v2 sprites preserve typed index/palette data beside the rendered canvas, allowing provider/renderer code to rebuild a sprite canvas with a loaded character palette.
- SFF v2 unsupported format counts are surfaced in diagnostics and compatibility reports.
- Unsupported or undecodable sprites fall back to mock sprites through `SpriteProvider` so inspection can continue.

## ACT

- `pal1` through `pal12` entries resolved from DEF are parsed as Adobe ACT palettes when present.
- ACT RGB entries are exposed as color strings plus raw 768-byte palette data; optional Adobe footer color-count and transparent-index metadata is preserved.
- Loaded character palettes are assigned bounded palette ids as group `1`, index `1..12` for current `RemapPal` destination lookup.
- `CompatibilityReport.palettes` summarizes declared palette refs, parsed ACT palettes, total declared colors, and palettes with transparent-index metadata.
- `SffSpriteProvider` can apply a runtime `RemapPal` destination to decoded indexed SFF sprites by rebuilding the sprite canvas from stored index pixels and the loaded ACT palette. Missing ACT palettes or non-indexed sprites fall back to the original sprite without crashing.
- This is first-pass ACT/SFF indexed texture handoff only; exact MUGEN/IKEMEN source-palette semantics, SFF v2 palette-bank parity, helper/team/redirect palette ownership, PalFX blend ordering, and truecolor/PNG palette behavior remain unsupported.

## SND

- Channel `0` voice playback follows bounded hit cancellation semantics: accepted normal hits increment the defender's explicit `receivedHitSequence`; browser audio consumes each new sequence once and stops only that actor's active or pending channel `0`. Guard does not cancel voice, matching channels on other actors survive, and later voices can play during unchanged hitstun. Helper-as-defender breadth, exact simultaneous/multi-hit ordering, common/system/BGM ownership, KO policy, and perceptual parity remain unsupported.
- Browser playback scopes numbered `PlaySnd` / `SndPan` / `StopSnd` channels by runtime actor plus channel. Matching channel numbers from P1, P2, or helpers can coexist; replacement and numbered stop/pan affect only the emitting actor's channel. `StopSnd channel = -1` and explicit `stopAll()` remain global. Controlled AudioContext integration coverage proves two-actor coexistence and actor-local replacement. Exact free-channel allocation, channel `0` hit cancellation, common/system/BGM ownership, broader priority/mix semantics, and perceptual parity remain unsupported.
- First-generation visual helpers can resolve direct `HitDef hitsound` / `guardsound` expressions through the helper-local expression context, emit helper-side contact sound/FightFX events, and attribute the resulting typed `audio:playsnd` operation to the root player trace. Required helper direct-HitDef/persistence gates cover `S5,0/1/2/3` and guarded `S6,4`; HitBy rejection proves the operation is not emitted without accepted contact. Exact archive playback, channel/mix/timing semantics, nested helper ancestry, redirects, teams, and full helper audio parity remain unsupported.

- Header/version detection for `ElecbyteSnd\0` archives.
- Linked subfile table parsing with group/index lookup.
- Embedded RIFF/WAVE payload extraction.
- Basic WAV metadata: channels, sample rate, and bits per sample.
- Parsed SND archives are exposed in Inspector/Compatibility UI.
- `CompatibilityReport.sounds` summarizes parsed SND archives for package inspection: declared total sounds, decoded WAV count, unsupported/raw count, format counts, sample-rate counts, and channel counts. This is compatibility telemetry only, not playback parity.

- Runtime `PlaySnd` events can decode and play matching WAV payloads through Web Audio after browser user-gesture unlock. The browser audio adapter now scans player actor snapshots and effect actor snapshots so imported helper-local sound events are consumable without promoting helpers to full players.
- The partial Web Audio path tracks non-negative channels plus unchannelled sources: normal `PlaySnd` replaces an active explicit channel, `PlaySnd lowpriority = 1` skips when that channel is already active, `SndPan` updates an active explicit channel panner, `StopSnd channel = -1` / omitted channel stops tracked channelled and unchannelled sources, `volumescale` applies bounded gain scaling, legacy `volume` remains diagnostic-only, `freqmul` applies bounded playback-rate scaling, `loop = 1` enables source looping, and `pan` / `abspan` apply bounded stereo panning for decodable SND playback. Relative `pan` uses actor x, facing, and camera x; `abspan` uses screen-center offset. Exact priority classes, pre-RC8 legacy `volume` gain semantics, exact panning, timing, mixing, global channel fallback, pause/superpause audio behavior, and full MUGEN/IKEMEN audio parity remain unsupported.

## Stage DEF

- Stage `.def` discovery from ZIP/folder packages when files live under `stages/`.
- `[Info]`, `[Camera]`, `[PlayerInfo]`, `[StageInfo]`, `[Music]`, `[BGDef]`, and `[BG ...]` section parsing.
- Imported stage runtime mapping for display name, side bounds, camera start/zoom, player starts/facing, zoffset, and localcoord.
- Stage sprite/music path resolution from the stage folder, package root, and `data/` style fallbacks.
- Parsed `[BG ...]` sections preserve `id`, `spriteno`, `actionno`, `start`, `delta`, `layerno`, `tile`, and `tilespacing` metadata.
- `[BGCtrlDef ...]` and `[BGCtrl ...]` sections are parsed into Stage BG controller IR with group name, inherited `looptime`, inherited/per-controller `ctrlID`, controller type, timing window, params, and target layer ids.
- Recognized BGCtrl types are `Null`, `Visible`, `Enabled`, `VelSet`, `VelAdd`, `PosSet`, `PosAdd`, `Anim`, `SinX`, and `SinY`. They execute through a bounded renderer path for visibility/enabled skips, position/velocity offsets, action swaps, and simple sine offsets. Stage BG layers also preserve bounded `trans = none/add/add1/addalpha/sub` plus `alpha = src,dst` metadata, expose it in Stage reports/Studio layer rows, and map it into Three.js normal/additive/subtractive material params with bounded opacity for `addalpha`. Stage BG `maskwindow` and deprecated `window` also parse into bounded rectangular clip metadata and renderer-side clipped geometry/UVs. Exact MUGEN timing, side effects, color-zero `mask` semantics, exact `windowdelta`/zoom behavior, exact blend math, palette interaction, and full parity remain unsupported.
- Static normal BG sprites can render from the stage SFF when the referenced `spriteno` is decoded by the existing SFF reader.
- Embedded stage `[Begin Action N]` blocks are parsed for action-backed BG layers.
- Action-backed BG layers can render when their referenced AIR frames resolve to decoded stage SFF sprites.
- Basic horizontal camera parallax is applied from layer `delta`.
- Basic bounded sprite tiling is applied from `tile`/`tilespacing` so repeated floor/wall layers can fill the viewport.
- Stage compatibility summaries report DEF/SFF/music presence, decoded stage sprites, BG sprite coverage, animated BG coverage, tiled/clipped layers, bounded BGCtrl coverage, placeholder fallbacks, warnings, and known unsupported stage features.
- Stage compatibility reports now include a first per-layer BG IR: each imported `[BG ...]` layer records its source section, type, layer number, control id, start, delta, tiling, bounded transparency metadata, bounded clip metadata, sprite/action reference, decoded-frame coverage, unsupported layer features, fallback reason, and status as `rendered`, `animated`, `fallback`, `missing`, or `unsupported`.
- Stage compatibility reports include BG controller rows with bounded/unsupported status, timing, ctrl ids, resolved target layer labels, raw params, unsupported type notes, and fallback notes for exact parity gaps.
- Placeholder runtime background bands remain as a fallback when a stage BG sprite is missing or not decodable.

## Compatibility Profiles / IKEMEN Scanner

- Character compatibility reports include explicit profile metadata: `native-runtime`, `mugen-1.0`, `mugen-1.1`, and optional `ikemen-go-scan`.
- The first `ikemen-go-scan` implementation scans package paths and text files before runtime execution.
- Scanner-recognized IKEMEN-only features include `.zss` files, `.zss` state references, matching `.cns.zss` fallback files for CNS/ST references, ZSS `[Statedef ...]` / `[State ...]` code blocks, ZSS controller syntax, ZSS function/local-variable/loop/`ignoreHitPause`/`persistent` blocks, `.lua` files, `lua` / `luafile` / `luacode` hooks, Lua `hook.add` / `hook.run` / `hook.runFirst` calls, `config.json`, path-only screenpack `select/system/fight/storyboard/logo/intro/ending.def` files, screenpack `menu.itemname.*` entries, selected IKEMEN-only menu modes, select/story `unlock` expressions, `commandlist` and `movelist*` references, `IkemenVersion`, selected IKEMEN-only controller names such as `AssertCommand`, `AssertInput`, `AssertAnalogVector`, `Camera`, `CameraCtrl`, `ChangeMovelist`, `Depth`, `GetHitVarSet`, `LifeBarAction`, `GameMakeAnim`, `Text`, `ModifyText`, `RemoveText`, `RedLifeSet`, `ModifyPlayer`, `ModifyStageVar`, `ModifyBGCtrl`, `CameraCtrl`, `Dialogue`, `TagIn`, `TagOut`, `MapSet`, and `MapAdd`, selected IKEMEN-only controller params such as `RedirectID`, `F` fightfx animation prefixes, character-specific `fightfx.prefix` metadata, selected `AssertSpecial` flags, selected source-mapped extended trigger identifiers that are not in the current bounded runtime subset, model-stage assets, video background layers, and named 3D/Z stage params such as `topz`, `botz`, `ztopscale`, `depthtoscreen`, `zoffsetlink`, `startz`, `stagecamera.z`, `scenenumber`, `model`, `modeloffset`, `modelrotate`, `modelscale`, `attachedchar`, and `fov`.
- IKEMEN scanner findings are added to `CompatibilityReport.profiles.ikemen`, the exported compatibility JSON, the DebugPanel compatibility section, Studio Evidence, and the unsupported feature list as scanner-only facts.
- Scanner findings are labeled `Recognized + Unsupported`; no ZSS, Lua, rollback, netplay, model-stage runtime, or IKEMEN-only behavior is executed.

## CMD

- `[Command]` blocks with `name`, `command`, and `time`.
- `[Defaults]` `command.time`, partial `command.steptime`, `command.buffer.time`, and partial `command.buffer.hitpause`.
- Per-command `time`, partial `steptime`, `buffer.time`, and partial `buffer.hitpause` overrides.
- `[Remap]` button aliases are parsed before command tokenization; remapped commands show their original and resolved sequences in the UI, and blank remap targets disable the affected command path.
- Direction/button/modifier/separator/combo token classification.
- `CommandBuffer` stores inputs by frame, exposes a bounded debug history of recent samples, and can query active commands with duplicate-name alternatives.
- Hit-pause input samples can be buffered for commands that opt into `buffer.hitpause`; hit-pause samples are ignored for commands that opt out.
- Derived diagonals (`DF`, `DB`, `UF`, `UB`) from simultaneous cardinal input.
- Command matching collapses input into an 8-way direction so `DF` does not satisfy a plain `F` step unless the command uses `$F`.
- Optional private-fixture `kfm-official-qcf-x.json` checksum `349cd995` proves one real KFM `QCF_x` command route can buffer input, enter state `1000`, advance through ordered actor-frame `11 -> 20 -> 1000`, execute `ChangeState` / `PosAdd` / `HitDef`, emit move/hit `PlaySnd` telemetry `S0,3` and `S5,4`, inherit `[Data] sparkno = 2` for hit-spark telemetry with `sparkxy = -10,-60`, share contact package metadata between hit sound and spark, seed target link `p1 -> p2 / 0`, and finish with bounded hitfall/damage evidence. This is a single Kung Fu Palm route gate, not broad special-move parity, exact renderer/audio playback, or full effect parity.
- Repeated direction/button steps such as `F, F` require a fresh activation instead of matching a held input across adjacent frames.
- Plain direction/button inputs now require a fresh press/change within the buffer window instead of staying active for the full duration of a hold.
- Partial `/` hold matching for buttons and direction families, such as `/x` and `/$D`.
- Partial `~` release matching for buttons and directions, including common direction-release transitions such as `~D, DF`.
- Partial numeric charge matching on `/N` and `~N` modifiers, including command forms such as `~30$D, F, x`.
- Partial `steptime` matching rejects commands when consecutive matched steps are farther apart than the command's step window; when unset it falls back to the command's total `time`.
- `$` direction-family matching for commands such as `/$D`.
- Same-frame `+` button combos.
- Same-step `|` alternatives for directions/buttons, including alternatives inside a same-frame `+` combo such as `x+y|z`.

## Runtime Input / Movement

The gate requires imported actor-frame state/physics/velocity/airborne evidence and order `20 -> 10 -> 40`. This is sandbox input-control evidence only; exact MUGEN/IKEMEN Common1 movement states, CMD command priority quirks, command-buffer raw direction evidence, landing timing, collision/platform physics, AI behavior, and full movement parity remain unsupported.

The gate requires ordered actor-frame evidence `20 -> 11 -> 41` plus final state/action `0` with control. This is private fixture confidence only; public bundled KFM support, exact Common1 movement tables, CMD priority/raw-buffer parity, landing/collision/platform parity, visual parity, and full movement parity remain unsupported.

- `MugenCharacterLoader` caches one `RuntimeProgramIr` per loaded character. Imported runtime fighters carry that compiled program, and `PlayableMatchRuntime` uses cached `StateProgramIr` / `ControllerIr` for active-state controllers, State -1 setup/routing, and trigger evaluation. `StateProgramExecutor` now dispatches compiled controllers into change-state, change-anim, shared runtime-controller, side-effect, or unsupported families. `CompatibilityReport` derives compiled state/controller/trigger/routable counts from the same compiler report instead of maintaining a separate controller-support list. Imported runtime sessions also expose `executedOperations` so traces and exports can prove when side effects such as `HitDef`, `Target*`, `Pause`/`SuperPause`, `PlaySnd`/`StopSnd`, `Projectile`, `Helper`, `Explod`, `HitFall*`, `FallEnvShake`, static `EnvShake`, static numeric `VelSet`/`VelAdd`/`VelMul`/`HitVelSet`/`PosSet`/`PosAdd`/bounded `Gravity`, static `PosFreeze`/`ScreenBound`, static `Width`, static `PlayerPush`, static `StateTypeSet`, static `Turn`, static `SprPriority`, static `PalFX`, static `Trans`, static `AngleSet`/`AngleAdd`/`AngleMul`/`AngleDraw`, static `RemapPal`, static numeric `CtrlSet`/`LifeAdd`/`LifeSet`/`PowerAdd`/`PowerSet`/`VarSet`/`VarAdd`/`VarRandom`/`VarRangeSet`, typed `VarSet`/`VarAdd sysvar(n)` assignments, static `HitBy`/`NotHitBy`/`HitOverride` setup, static `ReversalDef` setup, and static plus resolved dynamic `AttackMulSet`/`DefenceMulSet` damage scaling came through typed `ControllerOp` data. Dynamic `AttackMulSet value` / `DefenceMulSet value` now records typed `damage-scale:*` evidence through `synthetic-imported-damage-scale-dynamic.json` checksum `3433b369` / final checksum `e3db6dd9` after runtime expression resolution. Static `EnvShake` params now lower into `envshake` operation evidence required by `synthetic-imported-envshake.json` checksum `061f17d5`; dynamic `EnvShake time/freq/ampl/phase` refs now record typed `envshake` evidence through `synthetic-imported-envshake-dynamic.json` checksum `e1bf593f` / final checksum `8f52f1f4` after runtime expression resolution. Static `HitBy` allow-list evidence is now required through `synthetic-imported-hitby-allow.json` checksum `c75d5c7d`, and static `NotHitBy` deny-list evidence remains required through `synthetic-imported-reject.json` checksum `5aca7dc0`; both are bounded hit-eligibility traces, not exact attr grammar or slot-priority parity. Static `PlaySnd` sound refs and `StopSnd` channels lower into `audio:*` operation evidence; dynamic `PlaySnd value`, dynamic audio numeric refs, dynamic `SuperPause sound`, and bounded dynamic direct `HitDef hitsound` / `guardsound` contact refs now record typed audio evidence after resolution while preserving raw sound-event telemetry. Static `HitDef` params now include bounded direct `kill`, bounded `guard.kill = 0` nonlethal chip clamp, bounded default `guard.kill` chip KO through required `synthetic-imported-hitdef-guard-ko.json` checksum `b7db75f4`, stored `fall.kill`, and bounded `hitsound` / `guardsound` refs so direct hit, chip guard, `HitFallDamage`, hit sound, guard sound, and round KO telemetry can be proven in traces; static `LifeAdd kill` also lowers into resource ops for the same bounded negative-life clamp. Remaining dynamic movement/bounds/collision/metadata/sprite-effect/resource/variable/eligibility/reversal/audio/presentation expressions such as `Const(...)` still fall back to runtime expression evaluation. Larger visual/combat side-effect controllers still run from parsed CNS params via `controller.source` until they move into dedicated typed systems.
- `RuntimeActiveControllerRunWorld` owns the current bounded active-controller scan-to-dispatch bridge after state lookup and trigger filtering: imported-state scans, owner-backed state data, `ignorehitpause` filtering, compiled controller dispatch creation, route execution, and stop-on-state-change all sit behind one named boundary before concrete state/runtime/side-effect hooks run. `RuntimeActiveControllerDispatchWorld` owns the bounded active-controller route order after that bridge: active state/animation mutation dispatch first, shared runtime-controller execution second, side-effect dispatch third, and unsupported fail-soft dispatch last. These are support/ownership boundaries only; they do not add new controller semantics, exact CNS VM tick order, persistent-controller semantics, helper/team/redirect scopes, side-effect ordering parity, or full active-controller parity.

- `EnemyNear` redirect support is deliberately bounded. - `SelfStateNoExist(n)` is runtime-backed in a bounded own-character form: it checks the current imported fighter's compiled/parsed state table and is trace-gated by `synthetic-imported-selfstatenoexist.json`. Redirected state owners, helpers, parent/root lookup, and exact IKEMEN/MUGEN lookup parity remain unsupported.
- `SelfAnimExist(n)` is runtime-backed in a bounded own-character form: it checks the current imported fighter's AIR action map and is trace-gated by required `synthetic-imported-selfanimexist.json` checksum `99930032`, where action `200` routes and missing action `9999` fails closed before state `290`. Redirected animation owners, helpers, parent/root lookup, common/FightFX namespaces, and exact MUGEN/IKEMEN lookup parity remain unsupported.
- `SelfCommand` is runtime-backed in a bounded own-character form: it reads the current imported fighter's command buffer like `command = "name"` and is trace-gated by `synthetic-imported-selfcommand.json`. Helper/team/redirect command ownership and exact IKEMEN/MUGEN lookup parity remain unsupported.
- `StageTime` / `GameTime` are runtime-backed in a bounded match-tick form and trace-gated by `synthetic-imported-stagetime.json` plus required `synthetic-imported-gametime.json` checksum `bab573f3`, where delayed `x` waits until `GameTime >= 4` before routing into state/action `294`. Stage scripting, exact pause accounting, replay/rollback timing, multi-round timer ownership, IKEMEN round-system behavior, and exact MUGEN/IKEMEN timing parity remain unsupported.
- `Ctrl`, `StateType`, `MoveType`, and `Physics` are runtime-backed in a bounded owner-context form and trace-gated by required `synthetic-imported-state-context.json` checksum `cb9c3d1e`, where `x` plus `ctrl`, `StateType = S`, `MoveType = I`, and `Physics = S` routes into state/action `295`. Helper/team/redirect metadata ownership, exact controller-loop ordering, persistent-controller parity, and full trigger parity remain unsupported.
- `Alive` is runtime-backed in a bounded owner-life form and trace-gated by `synthetic-imported-alive.json`: it returns true when the current actor life is greater than `0`. KO transition ordering, round-state lifetimes, helper/redirect owner life, and exact IKEMEN/MUGEN semantics remain unsupported.
- `LifeMax` and `PowerMax` are runtime-backed in a bounded per-character resource-cap form and trace-gated by `synthetic-imported-resource-max.json`: imported CNS `[Data] life` / `power` values feed initial runtime life, max-power clamps, and trigger evaluation, with fallbacks of `1000` life and `3000` power when absent. Lifebar scaling, team-mode scaling, power mode variants, redirects/helpers, and exact IKEMEN/MUGEN resource-cap semantics remain unsupported.
- `RoundNo` and `RoundState` are runtime-backed in a bounded single-round match form and trace-gated by `synthetic-imported-round-trigger.json`: current support reports round `1` and active fight state `2`. Intro/KO/win/round-transition states, team modes, and exact IKEMEN/MUGEN round-system semantics remain unsupported.
- `RuntimeTraceGate.requiredRoundFrames` can gate bounded `RoundSnapshot` evidence; `synthetic-imported-round-ko.json` checksum `bfd5f073` proves KO state, winner/message telemetry, observed timer evidence, and final P2 life `0` after a lethal imported `HitDef`, while `synthetic-imported-round-timeover.json` checksum `7d9f7907` proves bounded `timeover` draw/winner/message/timer evidence through a short `roundTimerFrames` fixture. This is sandbox round trace evidence only, not exact MUGEN/IKEMEN timer speed, KO slowdown, lifebar, intro/winpose, team, screenpack, or transition parity.
- `RoundsExisted` and `MatchOver` are runtime-backed in a bounded match-context form and trace-gated by `synthetic-imported-match-context.json`: current support reports `RoundsExisted = 0` and `MatchOver = 0`. Multi-round accounting, win/loss bookkeeping, team modes, and exact IKEMEN/MUGEN match lifecycle semantics remain unsupported.
- `MoveContact`/`MoveHit`/`MoveGuarded` are state-local bounded direct-contact counters. They return frames since the current state recorded matching direct `HitDef` contact, return `0` when no matching direct contact exists, reset on state entry, and can be cleared by partial `MoveHitReset`. Required `synthetic-imported-movehitreset.json` checksum `719c2cc7` proves a typed `contact:movehitreset` clears direct contact before a later `MoveHit >= 1` branch into state `263` can execute. `ProjContact`/`ProjHit`/`ProjGuarded(projid)` remain bounded projectile-contact markers for current owner/helper-local states. Required `synthetic-imported-helper-projcontactpersist.json` checksum `65639428` proves a helper-parented owner-side Projectile id `8895` can route helper-local `ProjContact(8895)` / `ProjContactTime(8895)` through helper `1300 -> 1302 -> 1301` after guard contact. Exact first-tick timing, redirect ownership, broader helper ownership, multi-target lifetime, projectile reset semantics, Move* interaction breadth, and MUGEN/IKEMEN parity remain unsupported.
- `ReceivedDamage` / `ReceivedHits` are bounded defender-local hit markers. They are set after a direct `HitDef` or bounded Projectile hit routes the defender into its current get-hit state, and are trace-gated by `synthetic-imported-receiveddamage.json` plus `synthetic-imported-projectile-receiveddamage.json` for `5000 -> 280` branches. Guard chip, target-controller damage, helpers, teams, exact lifetime, hitpause accounting, and full MUGEN/IKEMEN parity remain unsupported.
- `HitCount` and `UniqHitCount` are bounded two-actor direct-hit counters for the current owner state. They increment after direct `HitDef` hit contact, reset on state entry and partial `MoveHitReset`, and currently do not count guard contacts or projectile contacts. Static `HitAdd value` can add to the current state's bounded direct `HitCount` telemetry through typed `contact:hitadd` evidence, but it does not increase `UniqHitCount`. Multi-target uniqueness, helper ownership, combo lifetime, hitpause accounting, and exact MUGEN/IKEMEN parity remain unsupported.
- `RuntimeContactMemoryWorld` owns the mutable bounded contact-memory store for direct contact, hit counts, `HitAdd`, reversal markers, defender received-damage counters, and projectile contact/time markers. `PlayableMatchRuntime` injects it into fighter state for actor/state-number integration, while `RuntimeDirectCombatWorld` and `RuntimeReversalWorld` consume it for direct hit/guard, received-damage, and reversal marker writes. This is a runtime ownership boundary, not a parity claim.
- `RuntimeReversalControllerDispatchWorld` owns active-state ReversalDef controller dispatch into `RuntimeReversalWorld`: controller telemetry, typed `reversaldef` operation selection, raw fallback activation payload, operation telemetry, and activation handoff. `PlayableMatchRuntime` still owns trigger filtering, active-state order, current-frame hitbox lookup, and later counter-result state routing. This is a runtime ownership boundary, not exact ReversalDef parity.
- `RuntimeReversalWorld` owns the mutable bounded ReversalDef activation, active counter detection, bounded no-contact guard-distance rejection, and direct counter-result mutation for the current direct, authored walk-back guard-input, stand guard-input, crouch guard-input, air guard-input, custom-state, and Projectile contact paths. `PlayableMatchRuntime` still owns state-entry validation, target-state routing, and broader combat timing. This is a runtime ownership boundary, not exact ReversalDef parity.

- `RuntimeStunWorld` owns the current bounded hitstun/guardstun input-lock, timer/friction update, hitstun presentation-action request, imported hit-state moveType preservation, current-move guardrails, and non-imported idle moveType restoration. `PlayableMatchRuntime` still supplies concrete action/state predicates and broader state routing, so this does not claim exact guard recovery, helper/custom-state stun ownership, Common1 tick order, pause interaction, or hitpause parity.
- `HitPauseTime` is runtime-backed in a bounded actor-context form: expression and controller-param evaluation can read the current actor `hitPause` counter when a controller loop is actually running, and it defaults to `0` outside that context. - `HitShakeOver` and `HitOver` are runtime-backed in the bounded two-actor path: `HitShakeOver` becomes true after hit pause ends, and `HitOver` becomes true after hit stun/guard stun ends. This is enough for the current Common1 stand get-hit, fall-branch, stand/crouch guard-hit `150 -> 151` / `152 -> 153`, and bounded air guard-hit/landing walk-control `154 -> 155 -> 52 -> 20` gates, but it is not exact IKEMEN/MUGEN get-hit or guard timing parity.
- `InGuardDist` is runtime-backed in a bounded two-actor form: the opponent must have a current attacking move in a guard-distance window, the defender state must be eligible for the move's `guardflag`, the attack box is expanded by parsed `guard.dist` or a bounded fallback, and the expanded box must overlap the defender's current hurtbox. This supports explicit guard-start trigger evidence, a required far-reject gate where a too-small `guard.dist` keeps the defender idle/control, plus first bounded automatic guard-start and guard-end bridges for imported defenders holding back when defender-owned Common1-style states such as `120`/`130`/`140` exist. Optional official KFM auto guard-start/end gates now require ordered real Common1 controller/typed-operation evidence through `120 -> 130 -> 140 -> 0` when the private fixture exists. Separate bounded contact evidence covers air guard-hit `154 -> 155`; exact proximity guard, exact guard-end timing, guard effects, landing, and full air guard parity remain unsupported.
- Required synthetic auto guard artifacts now require minimum controller-event and actor-frame state order: `synthetic-imported-auto-guard-start.json` checksum `0c734290` gates P2 state `120` `ChangeState` `Guard Start Done` plus actor-frame `120` before `130`, and `synthetic-imported-auto-guard-end.json` checksum `d1dc0aa3` gates P2 `120` `Guard Start Done` before state `130` `ChangeState` `Stop Guarding`, actor-frame `120 -> 130 -> 140`, plus final `0`/control. - Controller type, triggers, and params.
- Basic typed fields: `type`, `movetype`, `physics`, `anim`, `ctrl`, `velset`.
- Partial numeric controller params can evaluate simple expressions, including arithmetic, comparisons, `Const(...)`, and state-type checks.

This narrows the older helper blocked scope: helper-owned custom state tables, throws, teams, exact helper hitpause/tick order, exact helper `HitDef` / Projectile lifetime parity, visual parity, and full helper target/combat/projectile parity remain unsupported.
- Helper-local redirect/bind/effect support is intentionally narrow: `RuntimeEffectLifecycleWorld` supplies the current owner runtime state as both parent/root, the current two-player opponent as `EnemyNear` context, and the current opponent id for bounded helper-local `Target(id)` / bare `Target` reads after explicit-id, default-id, or bare helper `HitDef` contact. `HelperSystem` clones those states into the expression context, and focused tests prove `Parent,Var(...)`, `Parent,StateNo`, `Root,Vel X`, `Root,Var(...)`, helper-local `EnemyNear,StateNo` / `EnemyNear,Life` / `EnemyNear,Pos X` / `EnemyNear,Var(...)`, caller-provided helper-local `EnemyNear(index)` / `EnemyNear(var(n))` reads when an explicit `opponentStates` list exists, arithmetic, boolean, and `IfElse(...)` branches/values. The same bounded owner/root context supports static helper-local `BindToParent` and `BindToRoot` position binding, with required trace evidence for both; the required gates assert `ownerBind` target and static offset payload metadata in addition to actor-frame position. Helper-local `Explod` / `RemoveExplod` / `ModifyExplod` / `Projectile` / `ModifyProjectile` / `ProjHit` support is static and visual only except for focused dynamic/omitted-bound `ModifyProjectile` tests: it spawns owner-side Explod/Projectile actors from helper-local params, records the helper serial as parent, can remove owner-side Explods by static id, can mutate helper-parented owner-side Explods by static id, can mutate helper-parented owner-side Projectiles by static id, can resolve bounded helper-local dynamic Projectile bounds through `Parent` / `Root` redirects in focused tests, can preserve explicit Projectile bounds when later `ModifyProjectile` omits bound params, and can read helper-parented Projectile contact markers for bounded helper-local branches. This does not claim broader indexed/team/helper-owned redirects beyond caller-provided `EnemyNear(index)` lists, player-state binding parity, nested helper ancestry where root differs from parent, team/keyctrl ownership, helper `Target*` mutation/multi-target parity, helper-owned custom state tables, throws, exact helper hitpause/tick order, helper-owned Projectile combat/contact beyond bounded target memory, exact `ProjContact` / `ProjHit` timing and lifetime, helper-owned effect namespaces, helper-bound Explod/Projectile timing beyond bounded static routes, redirect mutation, dynamic bind/effect/projectile params beyond focused `ModifyProjectile` routes, or full redirect/bind/effect parity.

Exact slot priority, attr grammar, helper/projectile/custom-state redirects, `forceguard`/`forceair` edge timing, and IKEMEN parity remain unsupported.

## Runtime/Rendering

- First-screen `Runtime Mode`.
- `MatchWorld` is now the public match runtime facade used by the DOM app. It delegates to the existing `PlayableMatchRuntime` while the world systems are extracted, so this is an architectural seam rather than full actor-world parity.
- `MatchWorld.getActorRegistry()` exposes the first actor registry over runtime snapshots, indexing player/effect actors by id, kind, owner, root, parent, lightweight lifecycle status (`spawned`, `active`, `removed`), per-tick lifecycle events, target-memory links (`targetLinks`) derived by `RuntimeTargetWorld` from actor target refs, TargetBind bindings, and owner-side BindToTarget bindings, plus `RuntimeEffectActorWorld` store summaries and `RuntimeTargetWorld`-backed target snapshots for debug/evidence surfaces. Runtime Debugger now renders that registry, target links, store counts, and next effect serials; the QA bridge exposes it as `window.__MUGEN_WEB_SANDBOX__.actorRegistry`; and `RuntimeTraceArtifact` frame summaries preserve `world.lifecycle`, `world.eventsThisTick`, `world.recentEvents`, `world.targetLinks`, and `world.effectStores` without changing behavior checksums. This is lifecycle/effect-store/target-memory evidence, not a full helper/projectile/explod VM, exact parent/root parity, or full target semantics yet.
- `ActorSnapshot` exposes `actorKind`, `ownerId`, `rootId`, and `parentId` for players, helpers, projectiles, and explods; `spriteOwnerId`/`spriteOwnerDefinitionId` remain separate for owner-backed animation/sprite rendering.
- Three selectable local fighters: Nova Boxer, Mira Volt, Rook Apprentice.
- Optional loaded-character Runtime route when the imported character has decoded SFF sprites and parsed AIR actions.
- All active local runtime fighters are atlas-backed through `public/characters/<fighter>/sprite-sheet-alpha.png` and `manifest.json.frame_layout`.
- Original Rooftop Dojo native PNG stage with floor, camera, side bounds, parallax asset layer, grid, and axis overlay.
- Training Grid fallback stage with floor, camera, side bounds, background layers, grid, and axis overlay.
- Imported stage `.def` packages can be selected in Runtime Mode and drive simple match bounds, camera, starts, static SFF-backed normal BG sprites, action-backed BG animations, basic BG tiling/parallax, bounded initial velocity and authored-order `VelSet`/`VelAdd`/`PosSet`/`PosAdd` motion, bounded BG layer transparency, bounded `window`/`maskwindow` clipping, composed `BGCtrl` start/end/controller-loop/parent-loop timing, a bounded `Enabled` animation clock pause, and fallback placeholder layers for recognized controller types.
- Native `BGCtrl Lab` is included as a smoke-test stage to prove bounded BGCtrl rows and visible nonblank renderer output without relying on external assets; it is QA evidence for the renderer path, not imported-stage parity by itself.
- Keyboard control for P1: arrows, A/S/D, Z/X/C, Enter mapped to distinct MUGEN-style input tokens.
- Touch control overlay on narrow/mobile layouts using the same runtime input tokens.
- CPU-controlled P2 pressure.
- Idle, walk, crouch, jump, punch, kick, and hitstun actions.
- Basic hitboxes/hurtboxes, hit pause, hit stun, knockback, damage, power gain, round timer, KO/time-over state, pause, speed control, and round reset.
- Imported Runtime route maps standard AIR actions to idle, walk, crouch, jump, and hitstun, and can use parsed CMD `[State -1]` `ChangeState` entries for basic attacks.
- Official KFM local QA currently verifies stand light punch (`x`) and Light Kung Fu Palm (`~D, DF, F, x`) reaching CNS states `200` and `1000` through the imported AIR/SFF/CMD bridge, bounded real KFM `x -> 200` hit sound telemetry `S5,0`, bounded real KFM `x -> 200` hit spark telemetry for `sparkno 0`, plus a default defender-owned Common1 entry where KFM as defender reaches real state `5000` after a HitDef without `p2stateno`, a bounded stand get-hit progression from `5000` to `5001` through `HitShakeOver`, then back to state `0` through `HitOver`, a bounded crouch get-hit progression from held-crouch prep `11` through `5010 -> 5011 -> 0` with KFM-specific frame and crouch slide controller/typed-operation evidence, automatic guard-start/end through real Common1 `120 -> 130 -> 140 -> 0`, stand/crouch/air guard-hit branches through real Common1 `150 -> 151`, `152 -> 153`, and `154 -> 155 -> 52 -> 20` held-back walk/control, a fall/ground-impact/bounce/lie-down route through real Common1 states `5000 -> 5030 -> 5050 -> 5100 -> 5101 -> 5110`, a bounded lie-down/get-up route that reaches real KFM `5120` and returns to `0` with control, a bounded air recovery-input route `5050 -> 5210 -> 52 -> 0`, a bounded ordered ground recovery-threshold route where `5050` with positive `hitFall.recoverTime` precedes `5200` with `recoverTime = 0` and then completes `5200 -> 5201 -> 52 -> 0`, bounded official ground-recovery controller/typed-operation order through `5050`, `5200`, and landing state `52`, and an optional ground-recovery priority mirror where generic air recovery `5210` plus lie-down states stay forbidden on real KFM data. These are private local fixture gates, not bundled public assets or full KFM parity.
- Imported basic attacks can derive damage, guard damage, pause, hit stun, guard stun, pushback, and hitbox timing from CNS statedefs and `HitDef` where the parsed data is simple enough.
- Imported `HitDef` and `Projectile` guard timing can now preserve simple `guard.hittime`, `guard.slidetime`, and `guard.ctrltime` values into the runtime snapshot, derive omitted values through `ground.hittime -> guard.hittime -> guard.slidetime -> guard.ctrltime`, and expose them through `GetHitVar(hittime)`, `GetHitVar(slidetime)`, `GetHitVar(ctrltime)`, and nonzero trace actor evidence. Imported direct `HitDef` contact can route bounded stand/crouch/air guard-hit states through `150 -> 151`, `152 -> 153`, and `154 -> 155` when the defender owns those states. The required stand, crouch, atomic-`DB`, and air guard-hit artifacts now also gate named controller/typed-operation order through `ChangeAnim`, `ChangeState`, `HitVelSet`, `kinematic:hitvelset`, `CtrlSet`, `resource:ctrlset`, and final `ChangeState`, plus synthetic actor-frame state/physics/body/push telemetry; stand and air gates also include bounded velocity evidence where the synthetic route exposes it, and the air route additionally pins the `VelAdd` gravity controller. Exact guard control tick order, including HitOver vs CtrlSet parity when derived timing is short, remains unsupported.

Negative `LifeAdd` respects bounded `kill = 0` and defender-side `NoKO` clamps. - AIR action playback.
- `RuntimeActorConstraintWorld` owns the current bounded actor constraint path for `Width` body-width updates, one-frame `PlayerPush`, `PosFreeze`, and `ScreenBound` projection, stage clamping, and body-push separation. This is runtime ownership for existing bounded telemetry, not exact MUGEN/IKEMEN player/edge/camera/team/helper collision parity.
- `RuntimeDirectCombatWorld` owns the current bounded same-tick direct `HitDef` priority win/trade mutation and direct hit/guard result path for life, pause, stun, velocity, hit vars, hit fall metadata, power gain, contact memory, received-damage memory, and get-hit cleanup. This is runtime ownership for existing bounded direct HitDef telemetry, not exact priority classes, throw, multi-hit, helper/team/redirect, or tick-order parity.
- `RuntimeHitOverrideWorld` owns the current bounded HitOverride slot ticking and redirect mutation path for direct and projectile combat, including required direct-HitDef/player-owned Projectile/helper-parented Projectile guardflag filtering, lowest matching slot-priority gates, and explicit `missonoverride = 0` custom-state slot-priority gates. This is runtime ownership for existing bounded HitOverride telemetry, not full attr grammar, broader custom-state guardflag/timing breadth, helper/custom-state redirect breadth, projectile/custom-state edge timing, or IKEMEN parity.
- Play/pause and step-frame controls.

- Runtime debugger, combat debugger, life/power meters, frame inspector, and console.
- Studio mode has URL-addressable internal surfaces (`Workbench`, `Assets`, `Inspector`, `Debug`, `Evidence`, `Modules`, `Build`). Workbench/Assets/Debug/Evidence/Modules/Build render the match runtime in the center viewport; Studio Inspector renders the AIR inspector runtime so selected actions, frames, sprites, and collision boxes are visible in-place. Workbench opens with a command center for readiness lanes, operator priority, surface jumps, and primary Playtest/intake/trace/compile actions. Studio Assets is the first Asset Library slice: project asset flow summary, provenance/status filters, URL-backed asset selection cards, asset triage metrics, selected asset detail, selected entry assets, playtest-entry replacement flow, source/runtime mapping, visual dependency graph, dependency drilldown, missing/partial reference summary, related evidence, attention queue, and QA bridge summary at `window.__MUGEN_WEB_SANDBOX__.studioAssets`. Studio Debug is the Runtime Debug Studio slice: actor registry, ownership index, live snapshot facts, imported CNS execution evidence, bounded command-buffer history, trace frame/gate links, exact Inspector State/controller deep-links, Inspector Command deep-links, and URL-backed `debug` lenses for overview, target links, effects/stores, pause/HitPause snapshots, and audio/envshake events over the same `MatchWorld` data exposed by the QA bridge. Effect actor snapshots now expose typed drilldown payloads for visual `Explod`, `Helper`, and `Projectile` actors, including bounded ids, age/removal, priority, projectile hit/guard/re-hit fields, and Explod pause/bind/scale flags. Target/effect/pause lenses can also read the latest `RuntimeTraceArtifact.world`/gate evidence to show target-link frame rows, target-link gate evidence including binding offset/remaining/frame data when present, effect-store frame rows, and Pause/SuperPause/HitPause evidence, with target/effect frame rows jumping to the Evidence scrubber. Studio derives a current project workspace summary and exportable/importable/browser-saved `project.json`-style manifest from runtime/import state, including playtest entry, asset provenance, module status, acceptance gates, local recent projects, and next module cuts. It can compile that editor/project manifest into `runtime-manifest/v0` with active/planned/missing module diagnostics, and Studio Build can export and preview a `runtime-trace-artifact/v0` smoke trace plus readiness rows for runnable, partial, blocked, and exportable states. Studio Evidence aggregates gate, asset, trace, compile, compatibility, and diagnostic records with all/attention/category filters, keeps a bounded in-session list of recent trace artifacts, persists trace evidence in browser storage, compares current and persisted artifacts, renders a metric/gate Trace Comparison Review plus a Trace Frame Scrubber with per-frame actor/effect/input/event deltas and World Delta stats/rows for `RuntimeTraceArtifact.world`, and exposes the same aggregate as `window.__MUGEN_WEB_SANDBOX__.studioEvidence` plus selected frame data at `.traceFrameScrubber`. Imported or locally saved manifests apply P1/P2/stage only when those IDs already exist locally.
- `runtime-manifest/v0` now includes a `contracts` report with shared engine contract ids (`input/v0`, `asset/v0`, `snapshot/v0`, `render/v0`, `audio/v0`, `debug/v0`, `build/v0`, and `qa/v0`), known active/planned module contracts, explicit allowed/blocked claims, and `verificationCommands.boundary = "pnpm check:boundaries"`. Shared core contracts forbid MUGEN/IKEMEN-only concepts such as `CNS`, `CMD`, `HitDef`, `round`, `helper`, `projectile`, `explod`, `target`, MUGEN command routing, and ZSS; those concepts remain scoped to `mugen-compat`. Studio Modules now renders the same consume/provide/blocked contract data, Studio gates/Build/Evidence expose the `architecture-boundaries` / `test:architecture-boundaries` import-boundary proof, `pnpm check:boundaries` guards future shared-core/platformer/engine contract leakage, and `pnpm qa:smoke` verifies the visible Modules surface, QA bridge, exported package runtime manifest, and boundary evidence record all carry the shared contract report.
- Studio Build can export an `export-bundle/v0` ZIP package containing `package-manifest.json`, `project/project.json`, `runtime/runtime-manifest.json`, Studio summary, source-runtime asset maps, evidence, build readiness, compatibility report, README, the latest trace artifact when one exists, browser-fetchable local assets such as generated atlas PNGs/manifests/QA files/MUGEN-lite templates/authored stage art, and current-session imported ZIP/folder source files from the in-memory VFS. Package asset records include bytes, SHA-256 checksums, source paths, package paths, source kind (`fetch` or `vfs`), and bundled/skipped/failed status. `project/project.json` includes `sourcePackages` records with `linked` or `missing` status, required imported paths, character metadata, imported stage metadata, and optional deterministic SHA-256 identity metadata. ZIP/folder imports compute a fingerprint over normalized VFS paths and bytes; source relink distinguishes `matched`, `changed`, `missing`, and `unknown`, preserves observed identity on a mismatch, and blocks clean export until a changed package is explicitly reimported. A legacy manifest without a fingerprint stays `unknown` until an explicit relink establishes its new comparison baseline. Persistent source handles and automatic background reacquire are still future work.
- `RuntimeTrace` can run scripted input frames against the match runtime and emit compact actor/effect identity, typed `Explod`/`Helper`/`Projectile` effect payload summaries, `MatchWorld` lifecycle metadata, effect-store summaries, target links, and per-tick lifecycle events when available, round and compatibility summaries, bounded controller-event timelines, new runtime log events, combat reasons, typed operation counts, match-pause snapshots, match-pause actor/effect advance and freeze summaries, sound-event evidence, hit-effect event evidence, per-frame checksums, final actor hit-fall metadata, and a final deterministic checksum. `evaluateRuntimeTraceGate` can verify actor source/kind, effect kind, routed states, executed states/controllers, ordered controller-event sequences by controller, optional controller name, and typed operation, active commands, event categories, required runtime event substrings, combat reasons, match-pause requirements, match-pause advance/freeze requirements by actor id/kind/owner, sound events by actor/type/group/index/channel/state, hit-effect events by actor/source/kind/spark/raw prefix/spark offset/selected AIR-frame offset and duration/state, world lifecycle event requirements, effect-store requirements, effect-payload requirements for typed Helper/Projectile/Explod fields, target-link requirements including binding offset/remaining/frame evidence, round-frame requirements including KO/time-over winner/message/timer evidence, actor-frame body-width/body-push/sprite-priority/palette-fx/palette-remap/facing/state-metadata evidence, actor-frame/final-actor `customOwnerId`, final actor state/control/life requirements, and simple final `hitFall` requirements from those traces. `RuntimeTraceArtifact` can serialize that evidence as `runtime-trace-artifact/v0` JSON with checksums, compact per-frame summaries including `round`, per-frame actor/effect field deltas including effect payload deltas, `world.lifecycle`, `world.eventsThisTick`, `world.recentEvents`, `world.effectStores`, and `world.targetLinks` summaries, final actors/effects including sound-event and hit-effect history, script frames, events, combat reasons, gate requirements, gate evidence, and gate results. Effect payloads, sound events, hit-effect events, bounded controller-event timelines, and body/sprite-priority/palette-fx/palette-remap/facing inspection fields are excluded from behavior checksums so richer inspection data does not drift existing gates by itself.

- Compatibility scanner reports now omit `PrevMoveType`, `PrevAnim`, `PrevStateType`, `SelfCommand`, `StageTime`, `ReceivedDamage`, and `ReceivedHits` from unsupported IKEMEN extended-trigger findings because those triggers have bounded runtime/compiler evidence; adjacent unsupported triggers such as `RedLife` still appear as scanner-only warnings.
